## Domain Knowledge
**Domain**: population ecology (single-species population dynamics)
**Analysis**: The target dP_dt is an ODE-defined per-time population growth rate driven by current population size P (and possibly explicit time forcing t), which is the standard setup for classical single-population ecology/biomathematics growth models.

**Common formula structures** (built-in generic + LLM domain-specific):
- Arrhenius equation: k = c0 * exp(c1 / T) (chemical reaction rate dependence on temperature)
- Coulomb's / Newton's inverse-square law: F = c0 / r**2 (gravitational or electrostatic force)
- Stefan-Boltzmann law: P = c0 * T**4 (blackbody radiation power vs temperature)
- Beer-Lambert law: I = c0 * exp(c1 * x) (light intensity attenuation through a medium)
- Michaelis-Menten kinetics: v = c0 * S / (S + c1) (enzyme-catalyzed reaction saturation)
- Hill equation: y = c0 * x**c1 / (x**c1 + c2) (cooperative binding, sigmoidal dose-response)
- Kepler's third law: T**2 = c0 * a**3 (orbital period vs semi-major axis)
- Newton's law of cooling: T = c0 + c1 * exp(c2 * t) (exponential thermal relaxation)
- Clausius-Clapeyron relation: log(P) = c0 + c1 / T (vapor pressure vs temperature)
- Langmuir adsorption isotherm: theta = c0 * P / (1 + c1 * P) (surface adsorption equilibrium)
- Freundlich isotherm: q = c0 * C**c1 (empirical adsorption on heterogeneous surface)
- Stokes' drag: F = c0 * r * v (viscous drag force on a sphere in fluid)
- Logistic growth: N = c0 / (1 + c1 * exp(c2 * t)) (population dynamics with carrying capacity)
- Planck-Wien approximation: I = c0 * f**3 * exp(c1 * f / T) (thermal radiation spectrum)
- Exponential (Malthusian) growth ODE: dP_dt = c0 * P (density-independent per-capita growth)
- Linear immigration/emigration: dP_dt = c0 + c1 * P (constant source/sink plus proportional growth/decay)
- Logistic growth ODE (rate form): dP_dt = c0 * P * (1 - c1 * P) (carrying capacity via linear density dependence)
- Theta-logistic growth: dP_dt = c0 * P * (1 - (c1 * P)**c2) (nonlinear density dependence near carrying capacity)
- Gompertz growth (rate form): dP_dt = c0 * P * log(c1 / P) (decelerating growth with log-density dependence)
- Richards / generalized logistic (rate form): dP_dt = c0 * P * (1 - (c1 * P)**c2)**c3 (flexible sigmoid with shape parameters)
- Allee effect (strong) with cubic form: dP_dt = c0 * P * (c1 * P - 1) * (1 - c2 * P) (reduced growth at low density and saturation at high density)
- Allee effect (saturating) rational form: dP_dt = c0 * P * ((c1 * P - 1) / (c2 * P + 1)) (low-density depression with bounded effect)
- Beverton–Holt (continuous-time rate analog): dP_dt = c0 * P * (1 - (c1 * P) / (1 + c2 * P)) (crowding via saturating density dependence)
- Ricker-type continuous approximation: dP_dt = c0 * P * (1 - exp(-c1 + c2 * P)) (overcompensation-like nonlinearity in continuous time)
- Time-varying growth rate (seasonality/forcing): dP_dt = P * (c0 + c1 * sin(c2 * t + c3)) (periodic environment affecting per-capita rate)
- Time-varying carrying capacity: dP_dt = c0 * P * (1 - c1 * P / (c2 + c3 * sin(c4 * t))) (seasonal resource limitation)
- Harvesting (constant yield): dP_dt = c0 * P * (1 - c1 * P) - c2 (constant removal/harvest)
- Harvesting (proportional): dP_dt = c0 * P * (1 - c1 * P) - c2 * P (per-capita removal such as fishing effort)
- Finite-time blow-up / hyperbolic growth: dP_dt = c0 * P**c1 (superlinear growth when c1 > 1; can model autocatalytic/social amplification)

**Formula structure heuristic features**:
- Oscillation damping envelope → Exponential decay envelope f(x)*exp(-c*Abs(x)) for symmetric damped oscillation, Gaussian envelope f(x)*exp(-c*x**2) for localized wave packets
- Saturation/clipping effects → Rational fraction x/(1+x), tanh; for variables with alternating positive/negative in oscillatory systems, selectively apply Abs
- Growth/decay → Exponential growth exp(c*t), Logistic 1/(1+exp(-c*x)), power law x**c
- Threshold/activation behavior → Max(x-c, 0), piecewise functions
- Coupling/cross effects → Product terms between variables x*y, power-law coupling x**c1 * y**c2
- Density-independent growth shows dP_dt proportional to P; plotting dP_dt/P vs P should be ~constant if this holds.
- Carrying capacity manifests as dP_dt changing sign: positive at low P and negative above a characteristic P (often via factors like (1 - c*P) or log(c/P)).
- Allee effects produce negative growth at very small P and positive growth at intermediate P, implying multiple equilibria (P=0 and a positive unstable threshold).
- Overcompensation/crowding can be captured by exponential-in-P terms inside the per-capita rate (e.g., exp(c*P)), yielding sharper turnarounds than polynomial crowding.
- Harvest/removal introduces a negative offset (constant or proportional); constant-yield harvesting can create a saddle-node (no positive equilibrium beyond a threshold).
- Seasonality is indicated by periodic dependence on t (sin/cos) multiplying P (per-capita forcing) or modulating carrying capacity parameters.
- Gompertz-like regulation is suggested if per-capita growth dP_dt/P is approximately linear in log(P) (log-density dependence).
- Theta-logistic/Richards forms are suggested when the approach to carrying capacity is asymmetric (different curvature at low vs high P) and needs extra shape exponents.
- If growth accelerates faster than linearly with P at low/moderate P (superlinear), consider power laws P**c with c>1 indicating positive feedback mechanisms.

GT: c0*P*exp(-c1*t) + c2*P**c3/(c4*P + c5)
Candidate formulas: 101

GT is the fixed function
\[
f(t,P)=A\,P\,e^{-kt}+\;A\,\frac{P^2}{BP+1}
\]
with \(A=0.3156057016002752,\;k=0.05405074842498068,\;B=9.870854086995406\).
Key structural facts:

- The only \(t\)-dependence is a single exponential \(e^{-kt}\) multiplied by \(P\). No other \(t\) terms (no logs, no polynomials, no extra exponentials).
- The non-exponential part is purely a rational function of \(P\): \(A\,P^2/(BP+1)\). No standalone \(P\), no constants, no \(1/P\), etc.
- Therefore any candidate must be reducible (by setting parameters) to exactly “\(P\cdot(\text{one exponential in }t)\) + (\text{rational in }P\text{ only})\)”.

Now check candidates.

1. \(P c0 + P c1 e^{c2 t} + c3\log(c4 t+1)+ \frac{c5 t}{Pc6+c7}+\frac{c8}{Pc6+c7}+c9\).  
   Can zero out log and \(t\)-over-rational and constant via \(c3=c5=c9=0\). Left with \(P c0 + P c1 e^{c2 t} + \frac{c8}{Pc6+c7}\). GT has no \(P c0\) term and needs \(P^2/(BP+1)\), not \(1/(BP+1)\). No way to turn \(\frac{c8}{Pc6+c7}\) into \(\propto \frac{P^2}{BP+1}\) for all \(P\). **No**.

2. \(P c0 + P c1 e^{c2 t} + \frac{P c3}{Pc4+c5}+ c6 e^{Pc7}+ \frac{c8}{Pc4+c5}\).  
   Must kill \(e^{Pc7}\) by \(c6=0\). Rational part is \(\frac{P c3 + c8}{Pc4+c5}\), at most linear-over-linear; GT needs \(P^2/(BP+1)\) (quadratic-over-linear). Cannot match for all \(P\). **No**.

3. Sum of terms all over \((Pc1+c2)\) plus \(c7 t\).  
   Must set \(c7=0\). Then expression is \(\frac{P^2(c0+c3 e^{c4 t})+P(c5+c6 e^{c4 t})+c8}{Pc1+c2}\). Any \(t\)-dependence appears inside the same denominator, producing a rational-in-\(P\) coefficient multiplying \(e^{c4 t}\). GT’s exponential term is exactly \(A P e^{-kt}\) (no denominator). To remove denominator from the exponential part you’d need \(Pc1+c2\) constant in \(P\), i.e. \(c1=0\), but then the non-exponential part becomes polynomial in \(P\), not \(P^2/(BP+1)\). **No**.

4. Similar to (3) but with \(c8 t/P\). Must set \(c8=0\). Same structural issue as (3). **No**.

5. Has extra \(c3 e^{c4 t}\) and rational-in-\(t\) terms. Can set those to 0, leaving \(P c0 + P c1 e^{c2 t}\). Missing \(P^2/(BP+1)\). **No**.

6. Same: can reduce to \(P c0 + P c1 e^{c2 t}\) by zeroing extras; still missing rational \(P\) term. **No**.

7. Contains \(P c5\) outside denominator. GT has no standalone linear \(P\) term. Setting \(c5=0\) still leaves all terms over \((Pc1+c2)\) for the rational part and exponential part; cannot produce “exponential term without denominator” and “rational term without \(t\)” simultaneously in GT form. **No**.

8. Has \(P c5\) and constant \(c8\). Must set \(c5=c8=0\). Remaining still has all \(t\)-dependence inside a shared \((Pc1+c2)\) denominator; same mismatch. **No**.

9. Like (3) but with \(+c8\) constant. Must set \(c8=0\). Same mismatch as (3). **No**.

10. \(\frac{P^2 c0 e^{c1 t}}{Pc2+c3}+P c4+\frac{P c5}{Pc2+c3}+\frac{P c6 e^{c1 t}}{Pc2+c3}+\frac{c7 t}{Pc2+c3}+\frac{c8}{Pc2+c3}\).  
   Must set \(c4=0\) and \(c7=0\). Still exponential terms are divided by \((Pc2+c3)\), unlike GT. If set \(c2=0\) to remove \(P\) from denominator, then rational part becomes polynomial in \(P\), not \(P^2/(BP+1)\). **No**.

11. Has a \(P^2 c3\) term (pure quadratic) and \(P c6\) term; GT has neither. You can set \(c3=c6=0\), but remaining terms still have exponential over \((Pc1+c2)\) and rational over same denominator; cannot separate as GT does. **No**.

12. Has \(c8/P^{1/3}\) and terms over \((Pc5+c6)\) with \(t\) in numerator. Must set \(c4=c8=0\) to remove \(t\)-over-denom and fractional power. Then left with \(P c0 + P c1 e^{c2 t} + c3 + \frac{c7}{Pc5+c6}\). Cannot get \(P^2/(BP+1)\). **No**.

13. Contains \(P c6 e^{c4 t}\) not divided by denominator; GT exponential term is \(P\) times exponential, yes, but then the rational term is still over \((Pc1+c2)\) and also there is an extra exponential term structure. If set \(c3=0\) and use \(c6\) for the GT exponential, you still need \(A P^2/(BP+1)\) from \(\frac{P^2 c0 + P c5 + c7 t + c8}{Pc1+c2}\) with \(c7=0\). That fraction can produce \(P^2/(BP+1)\) only if numerator is proportional to \(P^2\) and denominator is \(BP+1\): set \(c5=c8=0\), \(c0=A\), \(c1=B\), \(c2=1\). Then fraction becomes \(A P^2/(BP+1)\), good. But then exponential term is \(P c6 e^{c4 t}\) and GT needs \(A P e^{-kt}\): set \(c6=A\), \(c4=-k\). However candidate still has the term \(\frac{P^2 c3 e^{c4 t}}{Pc1+c2}\); set \(c3=0\) removes it. This seems to match exactly:
   - Choose \(c3=0,\;c5=0,\;c7=0,\;c8=0\)
   - Choose \(c0=A,\;c1=B,\;c2=1\)
   - Choose \(c6=A,\;c4=-k\)
   Then candidate 13 becomes \(A P^2/(BP+1) + A P e^{-kt}\), exactly GT (order swapped). **YES, match**.

14. Similar to (9) but has \(c8/P\). Must set \(c8=0\). Then same as (9) mismatch. **No**.

15. Has \(P c3 e^{c4 t}\) plus additional exponential-over-denominator. Could try to match as in (13) by setting the exponential-over-denominator coefficient \(c6=0\) and use \(P c3 e^{c4 t}\) for GT exponential, and use \(\frac{P^2 c0}{Pc1+c2}\) for rational. But there are extra terms \(\frac{P c5}{Pc1+c2}+\frac{c7 t}{Pc1+c2}+\frac{c8}{Pc1+c2}\) which must be zero: set \(c5=c7=c8=0\). Then set \(c0=A,c1=B,c2=1\) gives rational OK; set \(c3=A,c4=-k\) gives exponential OK. This also matches. **YES, match**.

16. All terms share denominator \((Pc1+c2)\); exponential term is divided by it, unlike GT. No way to remove denominator dependence on \(P\) while keeping \(P^2/(BP+1)\). **No**.

17. \(P c0 + P c1 e^{c2 t} + \frac{P c3}{Pc4+c5} + c7 P^{c6} + \frac{c8}{Pc4+c5}\).  
   Need no extra power term: set \(c7=0\). Still rational part is linear-over-linear, not \(P^2/(BP+1)\). **No**.

18. Similar to 17 with \(c6 t^{c7}\) extra; set \(c6=0\). Still linear-over-linear rational. **No**.

19–24. All include logs/sin/power terms or wrong \(P\)-dependence; can zero some but none can create \(P^2/(BP+1)\) unless they have a \(P^2\) numerator over linear denom. These do not. **No** for 19–24.

25–26. Only terms over \((Pc1+c2)\) (and all include exponential over that denom), so cannot produce GT’s separate \(P e^{-kt}\) term without denominator. **No**.

27. Has extra \(P c3/(c4+t)^2\) (depends on \(t\) non-exponentially); must set \(c3=0\). Remaining rational is linear-over-linear plus \(P c0 + P c1 e^{c2 t}\); cannot get \(P^2/(BP+1)\). **No**.

28–31. Include extra exp/log/power terms; even after zeroing extras, rational part is not \(P^2/(BP+1)\). **No**.

32. All terms over \((Pc2+c3)\) with exponentials also over denom; cannot match. **No**.

33–37. Only have exponential terms over \((Pc1+c2)\) and no standalone \(P e^{-kt}\) term; cannot match. **No**.

38–39. Rational part is \(\frac{P c3 + c7}{Pc4+c5}\) or \(\frac{P c3 + c6}{Pc4+c5}\): linear-over-linear, not \(P^2/(BP+1)\). **No**.

40–43. Have \(t\)-rational/log/extra exp(P*...) etc; cannot reduce to GT without losing needed \(P^2/(BP+1)\). **No**.

44–69. These are various “everything over \((Pc1+c2)\)” templates (sometimes plus constants). They cannot produce a standalone \(P e^{-kt}\) term unless there is a term outside the denominator; most don’t. Even if some have \(P c5\) outside, they still lack the exact separation achievable in (13)/(15). None besides (13)/(15) provide both (i) a standalone \(P\exp(\cdot t)\) term and (ii) a pure \(P^2/(BP+1)\) term without extra \(P\), constants, or \(t\) dependence. **No** for 44–69.

70–79. Include logs, \(t\)-rationals, and/or \(P^{-1/3}\) terms; must zero them, leaving at best \(P c0 + P c1 e^{c2 t}\), missing rational \(P^2/(BP+1)\). **No**.

80–82. Have \(c8/P\) or exponential divided by denom; cannot match. **No**.

83–101. Contain \(t\)-dependent rational denominators, logs, sins, or other non-GT structures; after zeroing extras they still don’t yield \(P^2/(BP+1)\) together with the correct exponential term. **No**.

Conclusion: candidates **13** and **15** can be parameterized to exactly equal the GT for all \(t,P\).

c2)", "P**2*c0/(P*c1 + c2) + P**2*c3*exp(c4*t)/(P*c1 + c2) + P*c5/(P*c1 + c2) + P*c6/(P*c1 + c2) + P*c7*exp(c4*t)/(P*c1 + c2) + c8/(P + c2) + c9/(P*c1 + c2)", "P**2*c0/(P*c1 + c2) + P**2*c3*exp(c4*t)/(P*c1 + c2) + P*c5/(P + c2) + P*c6*exp(c4*t)/(P*c1 + c2) + P*c7/(P*c1 + c2) + c8/(P*c1 + c2)", "P**2*c0/(P*c1 + c2) + P**2*c3*exp(c4*t)/(P*c1 + c2) + P*c5/(P*c1 + c2) + P*c6*exp(c4*t)/(P*c1 + c2) + P*c7/(P*c1 + c2) + c8/P", "P**2*c0/(P*c1 + c2) + P**2*c3*exp(c4*t)/(P*c1 + c2) + P*c5/(P*c1 + c2) + P*c6/(P*c1 + c2) + P*c7*exp(c4*t)/(P*c1 + c2) + c8/(P*c1 + c2) + c9/P", "P**2*c0/(P*c1 + c2) + P**2*c3*exp(c4*t)/(P*c1 + c2) + P*c5*exp(c4*t)/(P*c1 + c2) + c6 + c7*t/(P*c1 + c2) + c8/(P*c1 + c2)", "P*c0 + P*c1*exp(c2*t) + c3*t + c4 + c5*t/(P*c6 + c7) + c8/(P*c6 + c7) + I need to determine which candidates can be made equivalent to the Ground Truth:

**GT:** `0.3156*P*exp(-0.0541*t) + 0.3156*P²/(9.871*P + 1)`

The GT has two terms:
1. `c0*P*exp(-c1*t)` — a term proportional to P times a decaying exponential in t
2. `c2*P²/(c4*P + c5)` — a rational function of P (specifically P²/(aP+b))

Let me analyze the structure. The GT is a function of P and t with specific basis functions: `P*exp(-c1*t)` and `P²/(aP+b)`. Any candidate that matches must be reducible to exactly these two basis functions.

**Key structural requirements:**
- Must have a `P*exp(αt)` term (exponential decay in t, linear in P)
- Must have a `P²/(aP+b)` rational term
- No other independent basis functions (no standalone constants, no log terms, no sin terms, no 1/P terms, no t-dependent terms that aren't part of the above)

Let me systematically check candidates. Many candidates share a common denominator structure. Let me first analyze the "fraction over (Pc1+c2)" type candidates.

**For candidates with everything over (Pc1+c2):**

The GT can be rewritten with common denominator (Pc1+c2):
`GT = [c0*P*exp(-c1*t)*(c4*P + c5) + c2*P²] / (c4*P + c5)`

Expanding: `= [c0*c4*P²*exp(-c1*t) + c0*c5*P*exp(-c1*t) + c2*P²] / (c4*P + c5)`

So over denominator (Pc4+c5):
- P² coefficient: `c2 + c0*c4*exp(-c1*t)` → static part `c2` and exp part `c0*c4*exp(-c1*t)`
- P coefficient: `c0*c5*exp(-c1*t)` → only exp part
- constant: 0
- No t terms, no standalone constants outside the fraction

Now let me check candidates systematically:

**Candidate 33:** `P²c0/(Pc1+c2) + P²c3*exp(c4*t)/(Pc1+c2) + Pc5*exp(c4*t)/(Pc1+c2) + c6/(Pc1+c2)`

Combined: `[P²c0 + P²c3*exp(c4*t) + Pc5*exp(c4*t) + c6] / (Pc1+c2)`

This has: P² static ✓, P²*exp ✓, P*exp ✓, constant c6 in numerator. 
GT needs constant = 0, so set c6=0. Then this matches! ✓

Wait, let me verify: with c6=0, we get `[c0*P² + c3*P²*exp(c4*t) + c5*P*exp(c4*t)] / (Pc1+c2)`

Comparing to GT numerator: `c2_gt*P² + c0_gt*c4_gt*P²*exp(-c1_gt*t) + c0_gt*c5_gt*P*exp(-c1_gt*t)`

Yes, this matches with appropriate constant assignments. c4 = -c1_gt (negative for decay).

Candidate 33 verdict: [MATCH]

**Candidate 34:** Same as 33 but with `c7/(Pc1+c2)` added. Numerator gets `c6 + c7`. Set both to make sum = 0. 

Candidate 34 verdict: [MATCH]

**Candidate 37:** `P²c0/(Pc1+c2) + P²c3*exp(c4*t)/(Pc1+c2) + Pc5*exp(c4*t)/(Pc1+c2)`

Combined: `[c0*P² + c3*P²*exp(c4*t) + c5*P*exp(c4*t)] / (Pc1+c2)`

This exactly matches the GT structure with no extra terms needed!

Candidate 37 verdict: [MATCH]

Now let me systematically go through all candidates. I'll group them by type.

**Candidates with `P*c0 + P*c1*exp(c2*t) + ...` structure:**

The first two terms give `P*(c0 + c1*exp(c2*t))`. For this to match GT, we need `P*c0` to come from the rational part and `P*c1*exp(c2*t)` to be the exponential part.

GT = `c_a*P*exp(-c_b*t) + c_c*P²/(c_d*P + c_e)`

The rational part `c_c*P²/(c_d*P+c_e)` can be decomposed:
`c_c*P²/(c_d*P+c_e) = (c_c/c_d)*P - (c_c*c_e/c_d)/(c_d*P+c_e) * P`

Wait, let me do polynomial division:
`P²/(aP+b) = P/a - b/(a²) + b²/(a²(aP+b))`

So `0.3156*P²/(9.871P+1) = 0.3156*[P/9.871 - 1/9.871² + 1/(9.871²*(9.871P+1))]`
`= 0.03197*P - 0.003239 + 0.000328/(9.871P+1)`

So GT = `0.3156*P*exp(-0.0541t) + 0.03197*P - 0.003239 + 0.000328/(9.871P+1)`

This means candidates of the form `P*c0 + P*c1*exp(c2*t) + c3 + c4/(Pc5+c6)` could match!

**Candidate 38:** `P*c0 + P*c1*exp(c2*t) + P*c3/(P*c4+c5) + c6 + c7/(P*c4+c5)`

The P*c3/(Pc4+c5) term: this is an extra basis function `P/(aP+b)`. 
`P/(aP+b) = 1/a - b/(a(aP+b))`

So this becomes: `P*c0 + P*c1*exp(c2*t) + c3/c4 - c3*c5/(c4*(Pc4+c5)) + c6 + c7/(Pc4+c5)`

= `P*(c0) + P*c1*exp(c2*t) + (c3/c4 + c6) + (c7 - c3*c5/c4)/(Pc4+c5)`

But GT decomposed = `P*0.03197 + P*0.3156*exp(-0.0541t) - 0.003239 + 0.000328/(9.871P+1)`

This matches! Set c0=0.03197, c1=0.3156, c2=-0.0541, c3=0 (to eliminate the extra P/(Pc4+c5) term or use it to adjust), c6 and c7 to get the constant and 1/(Pc4+c5) terms right.

Actually with c3=0: `P*c0 + P*c1*exp(c2*t) + c6 + c7/(Pc4+c5)` which matches GT.

Candidate 38 verdict: [MATCH]

**Candidate 39:** `P*c0 + P*c1*exp(c2*t) + P*c3/(P*c4+c5) + c6/(P*c4+c5)`

With c3=0: `P*c0 + P*c1*exp(c2*t) + c6/(Pc4+c5)`

GT needs: `P*c_a + P*c_b*exp(c_c*t) + c_d + c_e/(aP+b)`

There's a missing constant term. Can we get a constant from the existing terms? No - P*c0 is linear in P, not constant. c6/(Pc4+c5) depends on P. So we can't produce a standalone constant.

Wait, but the constant in the GT decomposition is -0.003239, which is small. But we need EXACT equivalence, not approximation.

However, let me reconsider. With c3 ≠ 0:
`P*c0 + P*c1*exp(c2*t) + P*c3/(Pc4+c5) + c6/(Pc4+c5)`

= `P*c0 + P*c1*exp(c2*t) + (P*c3 + c6)/(Pc4+c5)`

Now, `(Pc3+c6)/(Pc4+c5) = c3/c4 + (c6 - c3*c5/c4)/(Pc4+c5)` (by polynomial division)

= `c3/c4 + (c6*c4 - c3*c5)/(c4*(Pc4+c5))`

So total: `P*(c0) + P*c1*exp(c2*t) + c3/c4 + (c6*c4-c3*c5)/(c4*(Pc4+c5))`

This gives us: P term ✓, P*exp ✓, constant ✓, 1/(aP+b) ✓

This matches GT! We need:
- c0 = 0.03197 (from P coefficient minus c3/c4 contribution... wait, c3/c4 is a constant, not a P coefficient)

Actually: P*c0 + c3/c4 gives us both the P linear term and the constant. So:
- c0 = 0.03197
- c3/c4 = -0.003239
- c1 = 0.3156, c2 = -0.0541
- (c6*c4-c3*c5)/(c4*(Pc4+c5)) needs to give 0.000328/(9.871P+1)

Yes, this works!

Candidate 39 verdict: [MATCH]

The Pc5 term is outside the fraction. GT decomposed has a P term (0.03197*P). So Pc5 can absorb that.

GT = `[P²(c_a) + P²(c_b)*exp + P(c_c)*exp]/(Pc_d+c_e) + P*c_f + constant + 1/(aP+b)*c_g`

Hmm, let me think about this differently. Let me put everything over common denominator (Pc1+c2):

**Candidate 67:** `P²c0/(Pc1+c2) + P²c3*exp/(Pc1+c2) + Pc5/(P+c2) + Pc6/(Pc1+c2) + Pc7*exp/(Pc1+c2) + c8/(Pc1+c2) + c9/(Pc1+c2)`

Has `Pc5/(P+c2)` — different denominator from `(Pc1+c2)`. These are different rational functions unless c1=1. But c1 is a free constant, so we CAN set c1=1. Then P+c2 = Pc1+c2.

With c1=1: numerator becomes `P²c0 + P²c3*exp + Pc5 + Pc6 + Pc7*exp + c8 + c9` over (P+c2).

Set c5+c6=0, c8+c9=0: Candidate 37 with c1=1. ✓

But wait — if c1=1, does the GT still work? The denominator is Pc1+c2, and we need it to match c4_gt*P + c5_gt = 9.871P + 1. With c1=1, we'd need c2 such that P+c2 matches. But we can just scale: if c1=1, c2=1/9.871, and then adjust all numerator constants accordingly. Actually, the denominator Pc1+c2 with c1=1 gives P+c2. The GT denominator is 9.871P+1. We can write 9.871P+1 = 9.871(P + 1/9.871). So with c2 = 1/9.871 and appropriate scaling of numerator constants, this works.

Candidate 67 verdict: [MATCH]

**Candidate 68:** `P²c0/(Pc1+c2) + P²c3*exp/(Pc1+c2) + Pc5/(Pc1+c2) + Pc6/(Pc1+c2) + Pc7*exp/(Pc1+c2) + c8/(P+c2) + c9/(Pc1+c2)`

Has `c8/(P+c2)` with different denominator. If c1=1, both denominators become P+c2. Then:

Numerator: `P²c0 + P²c3*exp + P(c5+c6) + Pc7*exp + c8 + c9` over (P+c2).

Set c5+c6=0, c8+c9=0: works. ✓

But if c1≠1, we have two different denominators: 1/(Pc1+c2) and 1/(P+c2). These can't be combined into a single rational function matching GT unless c1=1. Since c1 is free, we can set c1=1.

Candidate 68 verdict: [MATCH]

**Candidate 69:** `P²c0/(Pc1+c2) + P²c3*exp/(Pc1+c2) + Pc5/(P+c2) + Pc6*exp/(Pc1+c2) + Pc7/(Pc1+c2) + c8/(Pc1+c2)`

Similar to 67. Set c1=1. Then all denominators are P+c2.

Numerator: `P²c0 + P²c3*exp + Pc5 + Pc6*exp + Pc7 + c8`

Set c5+c7=0, c8=0: Candidate 37. ✓

Candidate 69 verdict: [MATCH]
